# Codex verification — Q1 capability-readiness audit (#941). VERIFY the load-bearing claims that drive the pre-Q1 fix list. NO SPEND.

A Claude Codex Workflow (6 grounded agents) audited POLARIS Q1 capability vs frontier DR (Gemini 3.1 Pro
DR, ChatGPT 5.5 Pro DR). The full report is `.codex/I-meta-002-q1c/capability_audit_report.md`. Before
we file fix issues + tell the operator Q1 is "READY-WITH-GAPS", VERIFY these load-bearing claims by
reading the actual code. Each, if true, drives real work — so confirm or refute precisely.

## Claims to verify (read the files)
1. **C1 — depth cap + unwired deepener.** `scripts/run_honest_sweep_r3.py` defaults
   `PG_SWEEP_FETCH_CAP=20` (≈line 1591-1593) so the launch sweep tops out ~20 sources/question. AND the
   real depth engines — `src/polaris_graph/agents/evidence_deepener.py` (150-cap citation snowball) and
   the agentic searcher in `src/polaris_graph/state.py`/`searcher.py` (12-round/~96-query, STORM) — are
   wired ONLY into `src/polaris_graph/graph.py` (Pipeline B), with ZERO references in
   `run_honest_sweep_r3.py`. VERIFY: grep `run_honest_sweep_r3.py` for `deepen_evidence|evidence_deepener|
   execute_searches|agentic` → should be zero. Confirm the cap and the non-wiring.
2. **C1 — no clinical backend.** `src/polaris_graph/retrieval/domain_backends.py` (~line 370-385) has NO
   clinical branch (comment "clinical: rely on generic Serper + S2"); no PubMed/ClinicalTrials.gov/Cochrane.
3. **C2 — retrieval tracking is presence-only.** `src/polaris_graph/benchmark/pathB_capture.py:142-151`
   `record_retrieval_attempt` stores only backend NAME strings in a set (no per-call query/return-count/
   URL ledger), vs the per-call `reasoning_trace.jsonl` LLM roles get.
4. **C4 — contradiction detector is numeric-regex only.** `src/polaris_graph/retrieval/
   contradiction_detector.py` (~575-651) extracts (subject,predicate,value,unit) and flags numeric gaps
   only; qualitative/directional conflicts (contraindication present-vs-absent etc.) are invisible. It IS
   wired unconditionally into the sweep (`run_honest_sweep_r3.py:~2075-2087`).
5. **C4 — 4-role gate off by default.** `run_honest_sweep_r3.py:~3214-3240` fires the 4-role seam ONLY
   when `PG_FOUR_ROLE_MODE` truthy AND a transport is injected; default sweep runs the legacy evaluator path.
6. **C5 — citation-integrity leak.** `src/polaris_graph/generator/analyst_synthesis.py:~107` scrub regex
   `\[#ev:[^\]]*\]` matches only the `[#ev:...]` form, NOT bare `[ev_NNN]`, so a dangling `[ev_012]` can
   leak into the published report. (Check the regex; the leaked-artifact claim is from one run's report.md.)
7. **C6 — KG is write-only (dead reuse).** `src/polaris_graph/memory/verified_claim_graph.py`
   `query_related_claims`/`find_contradictions` are referenced ONLY by the store + its test — grep `src/`
   → nothing reads the reuse pool back into generation; the only writer
   (`roles/sweep_integration.py` run_four_role_evaluation) writes then closes. So zero runtime snowball reuse.

2: 
3: Run-scoped capture of every LLM provider completion (all roles) + retrieval-backend
4: attempts, for the DR head-to-head gate. This module stores PLAIN DICTS; the runner
5: converts them to ``scripts.dr_benchmark.pathB_run_gate.LLMCall`` when calling
6: ``assert_post_run`` — so this module has ZERO dependency on the gate / scripts package
7: and the production hot path never imports ``scripts`` from ``src``.
8: 
9: Best-effort + gate-flagged: nothing is captured unless ``register_pathB_capture()`` has
10: been called for the current run, so when the benchmark gate is OFF the hot path pays only
11: one contextvar read. Capture NEVER raises (it must not break generation), mirroring the
12: I-gen-004 reasoning-sink pattern.
13: 
14: Served-identity provenance: ``build_response_metadata`` reads ONLY genuinely-served fields
15: from the provider response (OpenRouter ``provider`` / served ``model`` / ``system_fingerprint``)
16: and DROPS missing fields. Request-derived values are never substituted, so a response that
17: fails to report its served provider/model makes the gate fail loud (in ``assert_post_run``)
18: rather than silently pass on request-derived data.

560: # relative threshold is tripped, absolute threshold is an AND filter —
561: # both must exceed to flag (avoids flagging 0.01 vs 0.03 rel=66%).
562: PG_CONTRADICTION_ABS_THRESHOLD = float(
563:     os.getenv("PG_CONTRADICTION_ABS_THRESHOLD", "1.0")
564: )
565: 
566: 
567: def _severity(rel: float, abs_: float) -> str:
568:     if rel >= 0.25 or abs_ >= 5.0:
569:         return "high"
570:     if rel >= 0.15 or abs_ >= 2.5:
571:         return "medium"
572:     return "low"
573: 
574: 
575: def detect_contradictions(
576:     claims: list[ExtractedNumericClaim],
577:     *,
578:     rel_threshold: Optional[float] = None,
579:     abs_threshold: Optional[float] = None,
580: ) -> list[ContradictionRecord]:
581:     """Group claims by (subject, predicate, unit, dose) and flag discrepancies.
582: 
583:     Fix-1: grouping key now includes DOSE. A 2.4 mg weight-loss result
584:     and a 7.2 mg weight-loss result are NOT a contradiction — they're
585:     expected dose-response differences. They will only be grouped
586:     together if both happen to have no dose tag (e.g., a narrative
587:     review that doesn't specify dose).
588:     """
589:     if rel_threshold is None:
590:         rel_threshold = PG_CONTRADICTION_REL_THRESHOLD
591:     if abs_threshold is None:
592:         abs_threshold = PG_CONTRADICTION_ABS_THRESHOLD
593: 
594:     grouped: dict[tuple[str, str, str, str], list[ExtractedNumericClaim]] = {}
595:     for c in claims:
596:         key = (c.subject, c.predicate, c.unit, c.dose or "")
597:         grouped.setdefault(key, []).append(c)
598: 
599:     records: list[ContradictionRecord] = []
600:     for (subject, predicate, unit, dose), group in grouped.items():
601:         if len(group) < 2:
602:             continue
603:         values = [c.value for c in group]
604:         vmin, vmax = min(values), max(values)
605:         denom = max(abs(vmin), 1e-9)
606:         rel = abs(vmax - vmin) / denom
607:         abs_diff = abs(vmax - vmin)
608:         if rel >= rel_threshold and abs_diff >= abs_threshold:
609:             predicate_display = predicate
610:             if dose:
611:                 predicate_display = f"{predicate} ({dose})"
612:             records.append(ContradictionRecord(
613:                 subject=subject,
614:                 predicate=predicate_display,
615:                 claims=sorted(group, key=lambda c: c.value),
616:                 relative_difference=round(rel, 4),
617:                 absolute_difference=round(abs_diff, 4),
618:                 severity=_severity(rel, abs_diff),
619:             ))
620: 
621:     # Sort by severity (high first), then predicate
622:     severity_rank = {"high": 0, "medium": 1, "low": 2}
623:     records.sort(key=lambda r: (severity_rank.get(r.severity, 3), r.predicate))
624:     return records
625: 
626: 
627: def format_contradictions_for_user(
628:     records: list[ContradictionRecord],
629: ) -> str:
630:     """Human-readable plain-text summary."""
631:     if not records:
632:         return "No contradictions detected in the evidence corpus."
633:     lines = [
634:         f"Detected {len(records)} contradiction(s) in the evidence corpus.",
635:         "",
636:     ]
637:     for i, r in enumerate(records, 1):
638:         lines.append(
639:             f"[{i}] {r.subject} / {r.predicate} — "
640:             f"severity={r.severity}, rel_diff={r.relative_difference*100:.1f}%, "
641:             f"abs_diff={r.absolute_difference:.2f} {r.claims[0].unit}"
642:         )
643:         for c in r.claims:
644:             lines.append(
645:                 f"    - {c.value} {c.unit}   "
646:                 f"[ev={c.evidence_id}, tier={c.source_tier}]   "
647:                 f"{c.context_snippet[:120]}"
648:             )
649:         lines.append(f"    Action: {r.recommended_action}")
650:         lines.append("")
651:     return "\n".join(lines)

1: """
2: Contradiction detector — HONEST-REBUILD Phase 3.
3: 
4: Finds pairs of evidence statements that directly contradict each other
5: on the same (subject, predicate, numeric value) tuple. Surfaces these
6: to the user before synthesis so the generator cannot silently pick one
7: side.
8: 
9: ADDRESSES PG_LB_SA_02_CONTENT_AUDIT Section E-06: the pre-rebuild
10: pipeline found two conflicting efficacy numbers for semaglutide weight
11: loss (STEP 1: 14.9% vs STEP 5: 17.4%), and the final report cited only
12: one without disclosing the range. A reader could not tell whether the
13: disagreement was stratification, dosing, duration, or cherry-picking.
14: 
15: DESIGN:
16: This detector is deterministic and rule-based. It does NOT use an LLM
17: to decide whether two claims contradict because LLM-based contradiction
18: detection has known failure modes on numerical values (confuses 14 and
19: 17 as "roughly similar" even when it's a 17% relative difference).
20: 
21: Approach:
22:   1. Extract structured claims: (subject, predicate, numeric_value, unit)
23:      from each evidence row using regex on the direct_quote.
24:   2. Group claims by normalized (subject, predicate) pair.
25:   3. Within each group, flag numeric discrepancies > 10% relative
26:      difference OR > 2.0 absolute unit difference (configurable).
27:   4. Return a list of ContradictionRecord objects.
28: 
29: The caller (Phase 4 synthesis) inserts a disclosure line for each
30: contradicted claim: "Sources report X (ref A) and Y (ref B). The
31: reasons for the difference are [analyst note]."
32: """
33: 
34: from __future__ import annotations
35: 
36: import logging
37: import os
38: import re
39: from dataclasses import dataclass, field
40: from typing import Any, Optional
41: 
42: logger = logging.getLogger("polaris_graph.contradiction_detector")
43: 
44: 
45: # ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
46: # Numeric + unit extraction
47: # ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
48: 
49: # Percentage values. Captures the number + "%" or " percent".
50: # Note: \b after "%" fails because % and space are both non-word chars —
51: # use a non-capturing boundary or a literal end-of-token check instead.
52: _PCT_RE = re.compile(
53:     r"(?P<value>-?\d+(?:\.\d+)?)\s*(?P<unit>%|percent|pct)(?=\s|[,.;:)\]!?]|$)",
54:     re.IGNORECASE,
55: )
56: 
57: # Mass / dose values with unit.
58: _DOSE_RE = re.compile(
59:     r"(?P<value>-?\d+(?:\.\d+)?)\s*(?P<unit>mg|µg|ug|mcg|g|kg)(?=\s|[,.;:)\]!?]|$)",
60:     re.IGNORECASE,
61: )
62: 
63: # HbA1c points. "percentage points" uses an explicit trailing word
64: # boundary since "points" ends on a word char.
65: _HBA1C_RE = re.compile(
66:     r"(?P<value>-?\d+(?:\.\d+)?)\s*(?P<unit>%|percentage\s*points?)",
67:     re.IGNORECASE,
68: )
69: 
70: # Time durations
71: _DURATION_RE = re.compile(
72:     r"(?P<value>-?\d+(?:\.\d+)?)\s*(?P<unit>weeks?|months?|years?)\b",
73:     re.IGNORECASE,
74: )

484: def extract_numeric_claims(
485:     evidence: list[dict[str, Any]],
486:     domain: str | None = None,
487: ) -> list[ExtractedNumericClaim]:
488:     """Extract structured numeric claims from evidence rows.
489: 
490:     Each evidence dict should have 'evidence_id', 'direct_quote' (or
491:     'statement'), 'source_url', 'tier'. Missing fields are handled.
492: 
493:     BUG-M-202 fix (deep-dive R7): `domain` parameter routes to a
494:     broader predicate set for non-clinical queries. Default None
495:     preserves the union-fallback (original behavior).
496:     """
497:     claims: list[ExtractedNumericClaim] = []
498:     for ev in evidence:
499:         quote = ev.get("direct_quote") or ev.get("statement") or ""
500:         if not quote:
501:             continue
502:         predicate = _normalize_predicate(quote, domain=domain)
503:         if not predicate:
504:             continue
505: 
506:         # Fix-1 uses _find_value_in_context which returns the matched
507:         # window so we can store the endpoint phrase.
508:         in_context = _find_value_in_context(quote, predicate)
509:         if in_context is None:
510:             continue
511:         value, unit, ctx_window, anchor_pos = in_context
512: 
513:         # R-5 Fix B: subject must be the drug NEAREST the numeric value,
514:         # not the first drug in the quote. Cross-drug comparison quotes
515:         # like "Zepbound 25.5% compared to CagriSema 23%" were mis-
516:         # attributing to the first drug mentioned earlier in the full
517:         # direct_quote (often the paragraph's primary topic, e.g.
518:         # retatrutide). _subject_near_position searches ±150 chars
519:         # around the value's position and picks the closest drug match.

164:     "policy": _EFFICACY_PREDICATES_POLICY,
165:     "due_diligence": _EFFICACY_PREDICATES_DD,
166: }

169: @dataclass
170: class ExtractedNumericClaim:
171:     """A claim like 'X causes Y-value-unit change in Z' extracted from evidence."""
172: 
173:     evidence_id: str
174:     subject: str      # e.g., "semaglutide"
175:     predicate: str    # e.g., "weight loss"
176:     value: float
177:     unit: str         # "%", "mg", "weeks", etc.
178:     context_snippet: str  # original text for display
179:     source_url: str = ""
180:     source_tier: str = ""
181:     dose: str = ""             # "2.4 mg", "7.2 mg", or "" if not present
182:     arm: str = "treatment"     # "treatment", "placebo", "comparator"
183:     endpoint_phrase: str = ""  # e.g., "at week 68", "from baseline", "mean change"

187: class ContradictionRecord:

194:     absolute_difference: float
195:     severity: str                   # "low" / "medium" / "high"
196:     recommended_action: str = (
197:         "Disclose both values with their source tiers in the final report. "
198:         "If one source is T1 (RCT) and another is T5 (industry), note the "

When IF is combined with structured physical exercise, the weight reduction relative to a control diet plus exercise reaches a weighted mean difference of −1.83 kg (P = 0.001) [CITE:ev_749f00cb5c5eea28], suggesting an additive effect when caloric timing is paired with energy expenditure. The largest effect size is observed with modified alternate-day fasting, which produced a weight reduction of −5.18 kg (95% CI: −7.04 to −3.32) compared with a usual diet, supported by high certainty of evidence [CITE:ev_e7bdb4797d3f6f0f]. The differential between these protocols is clinically meaningful: a five-kilogram loss falls within the range associated with measurable improvements in HbA1c and insulin sensitivity, whereas sub-kilogram fat-mass reductions, although statistically significant, may yield more modest glycemic benefits.
tests\fixtures\subagent_prompts\section_writer_response.txt:7:The pattern of fat redistribution is equally important. Beyond aggregate weight loss, IF is associated with a modification of the distribution of abdominal fat in people with obesity and T2DM, alongside improvements in glycemic control [CITE:ev_dde1177bb61ef9e9]. Because visceral adiposity is a stronger predictor of hepatic insulin resistance than total body weight, the redistribution pattern offers a plausible mechanistic bridge between fasting-induced energy deficits and downstream glycemic improvements relevant to T2DM management.
tests\fixtures\subagent_prompts\section_writer_response.txt:11:The lipid response to IF reinforces its cardiometabolic relevance for the T2DM population, where dyslipidemia is a frequent comorbidity. Across umbrella-review syntheses, IF reduced low-density lipoprotein cholesterol by a standardized mean difference of −0.20 (95% CI: −0.38 to −0.02; p = 0.027) compared with a non-intervention diet [CITE:ev_410655e66705beb6]. When IF is combined with exercise, the reduction is larger and reported in absolute units: a weighted mean difference of −5.35 mg/dL (P = 0.03) for LDL cholesterol [CITE:ev_39b4891376876856]. Triacylglycerols also fall under IF protocols, with a standardized mean difference of −0.23 (95% CI: −0.39 to −0.06; p = 0.007) [CITE:ev_e273c28dab55ecd8]. The convergence of LDL and triglyceride reductions is consistent with the broader observation that IF exerts beneficial effects on the lipid profile [CITE:ev_dde1177bb61ef9e9], a finding that strengthens its candidacy as an adjunctive intervention for individuals with T2DM whose treatment goals extend beyond glycemic control to encompass cardiovascular risk attenuation.

src/polaris_graph/generator\multi_section_generator.py:709:10. **Multi-source citation (M-27, for DR-grade citation density)**: When MULTIPLE evidence rows independently support the same claim, cite ALL of them, not just one. Example: "Tirzepatide reduced HbA1c 2.0-2.4% vs placebo across phase 3 trials [ev_012][ev_034][ev_055][ev_088]." rather than citing one ev_id. This raises citation density from ~1 per sentence to 2-4 per sentence where evidence supports it — top-tier DR (GPT-5.4 DR / Gemini 3.1 Pro DR) routinely reaches 50-200 citations for a clinical question by synthesizing multiple converging sources into each sentence, not by writing more sentences.
src/polaris_graph/generator\multi_section_generator.py:710:11. **Jurisdictional precision (M-29, for multi-authority synthesis)**: When citing regulatory, standards-setting, or governance sources from more than one jurisdiction (different countries, agencies, courts, or rulemaking bodies), attribute every specific assertion to the ONE jurisdiction whose source supports it. Do NOT use generic plural language like "both agencies", "all regulators", "authorities generally", "regulators require", "jurisdictions mandate", or similar when the evidence you cite comes from a single jurisdiction. A boxed warning in one jurisdiction is not the same legal instrument as a precaution in another jurisdiction; a formal contraindication in one framework is not automatically equivalent to a warning in another. If the evidence supports only one jurisdiction's position, write: "Jurisdiction A's framework classifies X as a contraindication [ev_A]. Jurisdiction B's framework addresses X through warnings and precautions [ev_B]." Only collapse to "both" / "all" / "generally" when you have a citation from each referenced jurisdiction in the SAME sentence proving the shared position.
src/polaris_graph/generator\multi_section_generator.py:712:12. **Primary-study framing (M-32, for claim-frame rigor)**: When you name a primary study, trial, cohort, experiment, or any individually identifiable empirical data source, and the cited evidence rows contain the structured metadata, provide the study's FULL FRAME in the FIRST sentence that introduces it: (a) sample size or cohort size (e.g. N=1879), (b) baseline value of the outcome being discussed (e.g. mean baseline [PRIMARY_METRIC]=[VALUE], baseline [SECONDARY_METRIC]=[VALUE]), (c) comparator / control / background condition (e.g. versus [COMPARATOR], versus placebo on [BACKGROUND], versus standard [REFERENCE_CONDITION]), and (d) the primary endpoint + timepoint (e.g. [ENDPOINT] change at [TIMEPOINT], [N-YEAR] [OUTCOME_TYPE], cycle-life to [THRESHOLD] retention). If the evidence row carries this structured metadata, you MUST emit it in that first sentence — do not compress N/baseline/endpoint into a single percent-reduction when the evidence carries the full frame. This is what distinguishes a research-grade deep synthesis from a news-style summary. Example template: "In [STUDY NAME], [STUDY_DESIGN_SUMMARY] randomized N=[SAMPLE_SIZE] participants with baseline [OUTCOME]=[BASELINE_VALUE] to [INTERVENTION] versus [COMPARATOR]; [PRIMARY_ENDPOINT] at [TIMEPOINT] was [RESULT] [ev_X]." Subsequent sentences about the same study may reference it by short name without re-framing. Generalizable beyond clinical: a materials paper gets composition + baseline performance + test condition + measured outcome; a cohort study gets population + baseline metric + intervention + outcome; a financial filing gets period + baseline metric + policy/benchmark + reported outcome.
src/polaris_graph/generator\multi_section_generator.py:713:12b. **Claim-frame hard constraint (M-38, eliminating under-framed study mentions)**: Rule #12 is asymmetric and STRICT — when you name a specific study, trial, cohort, or experiment by its short name (phase-N trial identifier in clinical; long-run battery cycling test in materials; named longitudinal cohort in epidemiology; named regulatory docket in policy), that sentence — or the IMMEDIATELY PRECEDING sentence in the same paragraph — MUST carry at LEAST THREE frame elements drawn from: sample size / cohort N; baseline value; comparator / control arm; specific dose or intervention level; primary endpoint; timepoint; effect size WITH uncertainty (CI, SD, or p-value). If you cannot produce three of those elements from the cited evidence, DO NOT name the study by its short name — phrase the sentence generically as "one randomized trial showed ... [ev_X]" or "a prospective cohort in the target population reported ... [ev_X]" or "one pooled analysis found ... [ev_X]" or "a long-run cycling test reported ... [ev_X]" instead. This hard floor prevents the failure mode where a sentence names a specific study but gives only a single effect-size number without N, baseline, or comparator — producing a news-style summary mis-labelled with a primary-study name. Concrete templates (use placeholders): GOOD: "In [STUDY NAME] (N=[SAMPLE_SIZE], baseline [PRIMARY_METRIC]=[BASELINE_VALUE]), [INTERVENTION_ARM] reduced [ENDPOINT] by [EFFECT_SIZE] versus [COMPARATOR_ARM] at [TIMEPOINT] [ev_X]." GOOD (generic when frame is unavailable): "A pre-planned pooled analysis of two phase-3 trials reported [ENDPOINT]=[VALUE] at [TIMEPOINT] [ev_X]." — no short-name attribution because pooled data lack per-trial N. BAD (under-framed, must be rewritten): "[STUDY NAME] showed that [INTERVENTION] reduced [ENDPOINT] more than [COMPARATOR] [ev_X]." — names the study with only one frame element (effect direction); rewrite as "A head-to-head trial of [INTERVENTION] versus [COMPARATOR] reported greater [ENDPOINT] reduction with [INTERVENTION] [ev_X]" which drops the study name because the frame is too thin. BAD (under-framed, must be rewritten): "[STUDY NAME] found median time to [THRESHOLD] was [TIMEPOINT] [ev_X]." — names study with only endpoint + effect; rewrite as "One pooled analysis of two phase-3 trials found median time to [THRESHOLD] was [TIMEPOINT] [ev_X]" ONLY if the cited evidence confirms pooled data across two trials. This rule is what converts a LOSE_BOTH on Claim frames into a competitive synthesis.
src/polaris_graph/generator\multi_section_generator.py:714:12c. **Anaphoric and group claim-frame enforcement (M-42a, extending rule #12b to bypass patterns)**: Rule #12b fires only on explicit short-name study tokens (e.g. specific phase-3 trial identifiers like [STUDY NAME]-N). Sentences using ANAPHORIC references ("This trial", "The same trial", "The study also reported", "That analysis") or GROUP references ("the [PROGRAM] trials", "the phase-3 program", "pivotal trials") bypass that rule and reintroduce the under-framed pattern. This extension closes the bypass:  (A) An ANAPHORIC sentence referring to a specific study must EITHER (a) include at least ONE frame element (sample size, baseline, comparator, dose, endpoint, timepoint, or effect-size-with-uncertainty) in the SAME sentence, OR (b) be placed IMMEDIATELY AFTER a sentence that names the specific study with >=3 frame elements (the antecedent provides framing context). A bare anaphoric sentence with no antecedent framing context is FORBIDDEN. (B) A GROUP reference like "the [PROGRAM] trials" or "the phase-3 program" does NOT inherit from a single prior study's framing. The sentence must EITHER (a) ENUMERATE the specific studies inline — e.g. "the [PROGRAM] trials ([STUDY]-1, -2, -3) pooled N=[SAMPLE_SIZE]" — OR (b) present a pooled / program-level claim with POOLED N AND POOLED effect size stated inline (e.g. "across the [N_TRIALS] pivotal trials pooled N=[SAMPLE_SIZE] adults with [CONDITION], [ENDPOINT] reduction was [EFFECT_SIZE]"). Both parts of the rule apply across domains: in materials/chemistry "these composites" or "the second-gen samples" inherit similarly; in policy "the CMS rules" or "the parallel rulemakings" do. Concrete examples (placeholders only): GOOD: "In [STUDY NAME] (N=[SAMPLE_SIZE], baseline [METRIC]=[BASELINE_VALUE]), [INTERVENTION_ARM] reduced [ENDPOINT] by [EFFECT_SIZE] versus [COMPARATOR_ARM] at [TIMEPOINT] [ev_X]. The same trial also reported [SECONDARY_ENDPOINT]=[VALUE] at [TIMEPOINT] [ev_X]." — second sentence is anaphoric but inherits frame from first. GOOD: "Across the [STUDY]-1, -2, -3, and -4 pooled population (N=[SAMPLE_SIZE]), median time to [THRESHOLD] was [TIMEPOINT] [ev_X]." — group reference with pooled N inline. BAD: "This trial also reported maintained [ENDPOINT] [ev_X]." — anaphoric sentence with no antecedent frame. BAD: "The [PROGRAM] trials found greater [ENDPOINT] reduction with [INTERVENTION] [ev_X]." — group reference without enumeration or pooled N.
src/polaris_graph/generator\multi_section_generator.py:715:13. **Policy-scope disambiguation (M-NEW-1, GH#422)**: When a paragraph names a specific program (Bill C-64, ACA, MACRA, EU AI Act, Article 34.7 CUSMA review, a particular budget line, etc.) and the evidence pool also contains projections / cost estimates / impact analyses for a RELATED-BUT-BROADER scope (universal single-payer projection vs phase-1 narrow program; comprehensive coverage estimate vs narrow amendment; multi-jurisdiction equivalent of a single-state rule), do NOT silently fold the broader projection into the narrow-program paragraph. When citing numbers from the broader scope, EXPLICITLY label the scope-attribution INLINE in the SAME sentence as the citation. Required pattern: write "PBO 2023 universal single-payer projection estimates the additional cost at $11.2B in 2024-25 [ev_X]" — NOT "the incremental cost is $11.2B in 2024-25 [ev_X]" inside a paragraph that opens with Bill C-64 phase-1 (which covers only contraception and diabetes medications). The decimal and the citation are correct; the missing scope label is what makes the conflation. Same evidence-ID, additional 4-8 word scope phrase before the citation. This rule fires regardless of which section the named-program paragraph appears in (Regulatory, Comparative, Economic, etc.). Failure mode this rule prevents: a reader concludes a narrow program will cost the broader program's projected figure. Concrete examples (placeholders only): GOOD: "Bill C-64 covers a defined set of contraception and diabetes medications [ev_A]. The PBO's 2023 cost estimate of a universal single-payer drug plan modeled on an expanded Quebec formulary projects incremental public-sector cost of $11.2B in 2024-25 [ev_B]." — distinct scopes named, decimals attributed to broader scope. BAD: "Under Bill C-64, the incremental cost to the public sector is estimated at $11.2 billion in 2024-25 [ev_B]." — cites the PBO universal-plan source as if it were a Bill C-64 phase-1 projection.

src\polaris_graph\generator\multi_section_generator.py:709:10. **Multi-source citation (M-27, for DR-grade citation density)**: When MULTIPLE evidence rows independently support the same claim, cite ALL of them, not just one. Example: "Tirzepatide reduced HbA1c 2.0-2.4% vs placebo across phase 3 trials [ev_012][ev_034][ev_055][ev_088]." rather than citing one ev_id. This raises citation density from ~1 per sentence to 2-4 per sentence where evidence supports it — top-tier DR (GPT-5.4 DR / Gemini 3.1 Pro DR) routinely reaches 50-200 citations for a clinical question by synthesizing multiple converging sources into each sentence, not by writing more sentences.
src\polaris_graph\generator\multi_section_generator.py:710:11. **Jurisdictional precision (M-29, for multi-authority synthesis)**: When citing regulatory, standards-setting, or governance sources from more than one jurisdiction (different countries, agencies, courts, or rulemaking bodies), attribute every specific assertion to the ONE jurisdiction whose source supports it. Do NOT use generic plural language like "both agencies", "all regulators", "authorities generally", "regulators require", "jurisdictions mandate", or similar when the evidence you cite comes from a single jurisdiction. A boxed warning in one jurisdiction is not the same legal instrument as a precaution in another jurisdiction; a formal contraindication in one framework is not automatically equivalent to a warning in another. If the evidence supports only one jurisdiction's position, write: "Jurisdiction A's framework classifies X as a contraindication [ev_A]. Jurisdiction B's framework addresses X through warnings and precautions [ev_B]." Only collapse to "both" / "all" / "generally" when you have a citation from each referenced jurisdiction in the SAME sentence proving the shared position.
src\polaris_graph\generator\multi_section_generator.py:712:12. **Primary-study framing (M-32, for claim-frame rigor)**: When you name a primary study, trial, cohort, experiment, or any individually identifiable empirical data source, and the cited evidence rows contain the structured metadata, provide the study's FULL FRAME in the FIRST sentence that introduces it: (a) sample size or cohort size (e.g. N=1879), (b) baseline value of the outcome being discussed (e.g. mean baseline [PRIMARY_METRIC]=[VALUE], baseline [SECONDARY_METRIC]=[VALUE]), (c) comparator / control / background condition (e.g. versus [COMPARATOR], versus placebo on [BACKGROUND], versus standard [REFERENCE_CONDITION]), and (d) the primary endpoint + timepoint (e.g. [ENDPOINT] change at [TIMEPOINT], [N-YEAR] [OUTCOME_TYPE], cycle-life to [THRESHOLD] retention). If the evidence row carries this structured metadata, you MUST emit it in that first sentence — do not compress N/baseline/endpoint into a single percent-reduction when the evidence carries the full frame. This is what distinguishes a research-grade deep synthesis from a news-style summary. Example template: "In [STUDY NAME], [STUDY_DESIGN_SUMMARY] randomized N=[SAMPLE_SIZE] participants with baseline [OUTCOME]=[BASELINE_VALUE] to [INTERVENTION] versus [COMPARATOR]; [PRIMARY_ENDPOINT] at [TIMEPOINT] was [RESULT] [ev_X]." Subsequent sentences about the same study may reference it by short name without re-framing. Generalizable beyond clinical: a materials paper gets composition + baseline performance + test condition + measured outcome; a cohort study gets population + baseline metric + intervention + outcome; a financial filing gets period + baseline metric + policy/benchmark + reported outcome.
src\polaris_graph\generator\multi_section_generator.py:713:12b. **Claim-frame hard constraint (M-38, eliminating under-framed study mentions)**: Rule #12 is asymmetric and STRICT — when you name a specific study, trial, cohort, or experiment by its short name (phase-N trial identifier in clinical; long-run battery cycling test in materials; named longitudinal cohort in epidemiology; named regulatory docket in policy), that sentence — or the IMMEDIATELY PRECEDING sentence in the same paragraph — MUST carry at LEAST THREE frame elements drawn from: sample size / cohort N; baseline value; comparator / control arm; specific dose or intervention level; primary endpoint; timepoint; effect size WITH uncertainty (CI, SD, or p-value). If you cannot produce three of those elements from the cited evidence, DO NOT name the study by its short name — phrase the sentence generically as "one randomized trial showed ... [ev_X]" or "a prospective cohort in the target population reported ... [ev_X]" or "one pooled analysis found ... [ev_X]" or "a long-run cycling test reported ... [ev_X]" instead. This hard floor prevents the failure mode where a sentence names a specific study but gives only a single effect-size number without N, baseline, or comparator — producing a news-style summary mis-labelled with a primary-study name. Concrete templates (use placeholders): GOOD: "In [STUDY NAME] (N=[SAMPLE_SIZE], baseline [PRIMARY_METRIC]=[BASELINE_VALUE]), [INTERVENTION_ARM] reduced [ENDPOINT] by [EFFECT_SIZE] versus [COMPARATOR_ARM] at [TIMEPOINT] [ev_X]." GOOD (generic when frame is unavailable): "A pre-planned pooled analysis of two phase-3 trials reported [ENDPOINT]=[VALUE] at [TIMEPOINT] [ev_X]." — no short-name attribution because pooled data lack per-trial N. BAD (under-framed, must be rewritten): "[STUDY NAME] showed that [INTERVENTION] reduced [ENDPOINT] more than [COMPARATOR] [ev_X]." — names the study with only one frame element (effect direction); rewrite as "A head-to-head trial of [INTERVENTION] versus [COMPARATOR] reported greater [ENDPOINT] reduction with [INTERVENTION] [ev_X]" which drops the study name because the frame is too thin. BAD (under-framed, must be rewritten): "[STUDY NAME] found median time to [THRESHOLD] was [TIMEPOINT] [ev_X]." — names study with only endpoint + effect; rewrite as "One pooled analysis of two phase-3 trials found median time to [THRESHOLD] was [TIMEPOINT] [ev_X]" ONLY if the cited evidence confirms pooled data across two trials. This rule is what converts a LOSE_BOTH on Claim frames into a competitive synthesis.
src\polaris_graph\generator\multi_section_generator.py:714:12c. **Anaphoric and group claim-frame enforcement (M-42a, extending rule #12b to bypass patterns)**: Rule #12b fires only on explicit short-name study tokens (e.g. specific phase-3 trial identifiers like [STUDY NAME]-N). Sentences using ANAPHORIC references ("This trial", "The same trial", "The study also reported", "That analysis") or GROUP references ("the [PROGRAM] trials", "the phase-3 program", "pivotal trials") bypass that rule and reintroduce the under-framed pattern. This extension closes the bypass:  (A) An ANAPHORIC sentence referring to a specific study must EITHER (a) include at least ONE frame element (sample size, baseline, comparator, dose, endpoint, timepoint, or effect-size-with-uncertainty) in the SAME sentence, OR (b) be placed IMMEDIATELY AFTER a sentence that names the specific study with >=3 frame elements (the antecedent provides framing context). A bare anaphoric sentence with no antecedent framing context is FORBIDDEN. (B) A GROUP reference like "the [PROGRAM] trials" or "the phase-3 program" does NOT inherit from a single prior study's framing. The sentence must EITHER (a) ENUMERATE the specific studies inline — e.g. "the [PROGRAM] trials ([STUDY]-1, -2, -3) pooled N=[SAMPLE_SIZE]" — OR (b) present a pooled / program-level claim with POOLED N AND POOLED effect size stated inline (e.g. "across the [N_TRIALS] pivotal trials pooled N=[SAMPLE_SIZE] adults with [CONDITION], [ENDPOINT] reduction was [EFFECT_SIZE]"). Both parts of the rule apply across domains: in materials/chemistry "these composites" or "the second-gen samples" inherit similarly; in policy "the CMS rules" or "the parallel rulemakings" do. Concrete examples (placeholders only): GOOD: "In [STUDY NAME] (N=[SAMPLE_SIZE], baseline [METRIC]=[BASELINE_VALUE]), [INTERVENTION_ARM] reduced [ENDPOINT] by [EFFECT_SIZE] versus [COMPARATOR_ARM] at [TIMEPOINT] [ev_X]. The same trial also reported [SECONDARY_ENDPOINT]=[VALUE] at [TIMEPOINT] [ev_X]." — second sentence is anaphoric but inherits frame from first. GOOD: "Across the [STUDY]-1, -2, -3, and -4 pooled population (N=[SAMPLE_SIZE]), median time to [THRESHOLD] was [TIMEPOINT] [ev_X]." — group reference with pooled N inline. BAD: "This trial also reported maintained [ENDPOINT] [ev_X]." — anaphoric sentence with no antecedent frame. BAD: "The [PROGRAM] trials found greater [ENDPOINT] reduction with [INTERVENTION] [ev_X]." — group reference without enumeration or pooled N.
src\polaris_graph\generator\multi_section_generator.py:715:13. **Policy-scope disambiguation (M-NEW-1, GH#422)**: When a paragraph names a specific program (Bill C-64, ACA, MACRA, EU AI Act, Article 34.7 CUSMA review, a particular budget line, etc.) and the evidence pool also contains projections / cost estimates / impact analyses for a RELATED-BUT-BROADER scope (universal single-payer projection vs phase-1 narrow program; comprehensive coverage estimate vs narrow amendment; multi-jurisdiction equivalent of a single-state rule), do NOT silently fold the broader projection into the narrow-program paragraph. When citing numbers from the broader scope, EXPLICITLY label the scope-attribution INLINE in the SAME sentence as the citation. Required pattern: write "PBO 2023 universal single-payer projection estimates the additional cost at $11.2B in 2024-25 [ev_X]" — NOT "the incremental cost is $11.2B in 2024-25 [ev_X]" inside a paragraph that opens with Bill C-64 phase-1 (which covers only contraception and diabetes medications). The decimal and the citation are correct; the missing scope label is what makes the conflation. Same evidence-ID, additional 4-8 word scope phrase before the citation. This rule fires regardless of which section the named-program paragraph appears in (Regulatory, Comparative, Economic, etc.). Failure mode this rule prevents: a reader concludes a narrow program will cost the broader program's projected figure. Concrete examples (placeholders only): GOOD: "Bill C-64 covers a defined set of contraception and diabetes medications [ev_A]. The PBO's 2023 cost estimate of a universal single-payer drug plan modeled on an expanded Quebec formulary projects incremental public-sector cost of $11.2B in 2024-25 [ev_B]." — distinct scopes named, decimals attributed to broader scope. BAD: "Under Bill C-64, the incremental cost to the public sector is estimated at $11.2 billion in 2024-25 [ev_B]." — cites the PBO universal-plan source as if it were a Bill C-64 phase-1 projection.

150:     def write_claim(
151:         self,
152:         *,
153:         claim_text: str,
154:         claim_id: str,
155:         verdict: str,
156:         role_verdicts: dict,
157:         timestamp: str,
158:     ) -> None:
159:         """Persist one claim outcome. ALL verdicts are stored (audit), only VERIFIED is reusable.
160: 
161:         `reusable` is derived solely from `verdict == "VERIFIED"` (anti-poisoning, Codex
162:         iter-2 P1-3): a non-VERIFIED row lands in the table for the audit trail but is EXCLUDED
163:         from `query_related_claims` reuse. `timestamp` is the caller-supplied audit time (this
164:         store never sources its own clock). `role_verdicts` (the per-role Mirror/Sentinel/Judge
165:         signals) is JSON-serialized for provenance.
166:         """
167:         reusable = 1 if verdict == _VERDICT_VERIFIED else 0
168:         self._conn.execute(
169:             """
170:             INSERT INTO verified_claims
171:                 (claim_id, claim_text, verdict, reusable, role_verdicts, timestamp)
172:             VALUES (?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?)
173:             """,
174:             (
175:                 claim_id,
176:                 claim_text,
177:                 verdict,
178:                 reusable,
179:                 json.dumps(role_verdicts, sort_keys=True, default=str),
180:                 timestamp,
181:             ),
182:         )
183:         self._conn.commit()

185:     def query_related_claims(self, claim_text: str) -> list[VerifiedClaimRecord]:
186:         """Return prior VERIFIED claims related to `claim_text` (the REUSE pool).
187: 
188:         ONLY rows with `reusable == 1` (verdict == VERIFIED) are eligible (anti-poisoning).
189:         Relatedness is a simple keyword-overlap match against the stored claim text (the
190:         contract only requires substring/keyword matching for reuse); an empty query keyword
191:         set returns nothing. Returns the eligible records ordered by recency (row_id desc).
192:         """
193:         query_keywords = _keywords(claim_text)
194:         # An empty / content-free query keyword set returns nothing (matches the docstring).
195:         # Without this guard an empty `claim_text` would substring-match EVERY stored row
196:         # (`"" in x` is True), returning the whole reuse pool (Codex sub-PR-5 diff P2).
197:         if not query_keywords:
198:             return []
199:         rows = self._conn.execute(
200:             "SELECT * FROM verified_claims WHERE reusable = 1 ORDER BY row_id DESC"
201:         ).fetchall()
202:         related: list[VerifiedClaimRecord] = []
203:         for row in rows:
204:             stored_keywords = _keywords(row["claim_text"])
205:             # Relate iff they share a content keyword OR one claim text contains the other.
206:             shares_keyword = bool(query_keywords & stored_keywords)
207:             substring_match = (
208:                 claim_text.lower() in row["claim_text"].lower()
209:                 or row["claim_text"].lower() in claim_text.lower()
210:             )
211:             if shares_keyword or substring_match:
212:                 related.append(self._to_record(row))
213:         return related
214: 
215:     def find_contradictions(self, claim_text: str) -> list[ContradictionFlag]:
216:         """Flag prior VERIFIED claims that the new claim may CONTRADICT (cross-time hook).
217: 
218:         Documented heuristic STUB (over-flags by design — a missed contradiction is the lethal
219:         error in clinical context): among the related VERIFIED reuse pool, flag a pair when
220:         they share content keywords AND EITHER their negation polarity differs (one negates,
221:         the other does not) OR they carry divergent numeric tokens (a dose/percentage
222:         mismatch). This is a REVIEW FLAG for the human / Codex §-1.1 audit, never a verdict.
223:         """
224:         new_keywords = _keywords(claim_text)
225:         new_negated = _has_negation(claim_text)
226:         new_numbers = _numbers(claim_text)
227:         flags: list[ContradictionFlag] = []
228:         for record in self.query_related_claims(claim_text):
229:             prior_keywords = _keywords(record.claim_text)
230:             shared = new_keywords & prior_keywords
231:             if not shared:
232:                 continue
233:             prior_negated = _has_negation(record.claim_text)
234:             prior_numbers = _numbers(record.claim_text)
235:             reasons: list[str] = []
236:             if new_negated != prior_negated:
237:                 reasons.append("negation-polarity mismatch over shared keywords")
238:             if new_numbers and prior_numbers and new_numbers != prior_numbers:

1: """Verified-claim knowledge graph (the snowball, canonical stage 17) — SQLite store.
2: 
3: I-meta-002 sub-PR-5. Persists every per-claim pipeline outcome and exposes a REUSE pool of
4: prior knowledge for later claims/questions in the same campaign. There is NO network here.
5: The store opens a SQLite file at an INJECTED path (default under a caller-supplied run dir),
6: and EVERY timestamp is passed in by the caller — this module never calls `datetime.now()`
7: (LAW VI: inject, do not self-source non-determinism).
8: 
9: Anti-snowball-poisoning (Codex iter-2 P1-3). `write_claim` persists ALL rows (including
10: FABRICATED / UNSUPPORTED / PARTIAL / UNREACHABLE) as AUDIT-ONLY records, but
11: `query_related_claims` returns ONLY rows whose stored verdict == VERIFIED. A claim that did
12: not clear the full Mirror -> Sentinel -> Judge fail-closed pipeline can therefore NEVER be
13: reused as prior knowledge — a hallucination cannot poison a later claim by being recalled as
14: "already established." The `reusable` column makes that filter explicit and machine-auditable.
15: 
16: `find_contradictions` is a cross-time contradiction-flag HOOK over the reuse pool. The
17: contract it owns is: surface prior VERIFIED claims that a new claim may contradict so a human
18: / Codex §-1.1 audit can adjudicate. The heuristic here is a documented STUB (shared keyword
19: overlap + a negation-polarity mismatch OR a divergent numeric token); it intentionally
20: over-flags rather than under-flags (clinical-safety: a missed contradiction is the lethal
21: error). It is NOT a verdict — it is a flag for review.
22: """

1: """
2: Evidence Deepener — closes the 25% gap to Gemini/ChatGPT Deep Research.
3: 
4: The remaining quality gap is NOT the LLM — it's the evidence depth.
5: Gemini writes better because it reads specific primary studies (RCTs,
6: landmark trials). Our pipeline only reads meta-analyses and reviews.
7: 
8: This module sits between `verify` and `evaluate` in the graph:
9:   plan → search → storm → analyze → verify → **DEEPEN** → evaluate → synthesize
10: 
11: Six operations:
12: 1. Named study extraction: LLM reads evidence, extracts referenced paper names
13: 2. S2 paper ID resolution: Convert source URLs → S2 paper IDs
14: 3. S2 citation chasing: Follow references from meta-analyses to primary RCTs
15: 4. S2 recommendations: Find related papers from seed IDs
16: 5. Mechanism keyword search: Targeted queries for HOW/WHY mechanisms
17: 6. Re-analyze: Fetch content, extract evidence, merge into pool
18:

1591: async def execute_agentic_search(
1592:     state: ResearchState,
1593:     client,
1594: ) -> dict:
1595:     """Execute searches via an agentic loop: seed -> search -> reason -> repeat.
1596: 
1597:     Each round generates targeted follow-up queries informed by prior results.
1598:     Converges when multiple signals indicate saturation or budget is exhausted.
1599: 
1600:     Returns state update compatible with the existing graph contract:
1601:     web_results, academic_results, status, plus agentic metadata.
1602:     """

1606:     sub_queries = state["sub_queries"]

1615:     research_notebook: list[dict] = []
1616:     already_fetched: set[str] = set()
1617:     last_analysis: Optional["AgenticRoundAnalysis"] = None
1618:     consecutive_empty_rounds = 0  # FIX: Track empty rounds to prevent degenerate loops
1619: 
1620:     tracer = get_tracer()
1621: 
1622:     for round_num in range(1, PG_AGENTIC_MAX_ROUNDS + 1):
1623:         # Budget checks
1624:         elapsed = time.monotonic() - start_time
1625:         if elapsed > PG_AGENTIC_MAX_TIME_SECONDS:
1626:             logger.info(
1627:                 "[polaris graph] Agentic loop: time budget exhausted "
1628:                 "(%.0fs > %ds) after %d rounds",
1629:                 elapsed, PG_AGENTIC_MAX_TIME_SECONDS, round_num - 1,
1630:             )
1631:             break
1632:         if total_queries >= PG_AGENTIC_MAX_QUERIES:
1633:             logger.info(
1634:                 "[polaris graph] Agentic loop: query budget exhausted "
1635:                 "(%d >= %d) after %d rounds",
1636:                 total_queries, PG_AGENTIC_MAX_QUERIES, round_num - 1,
1637:             )
1638:             break
1639: 
1640:         if round_num == 1:
1641:             # Use seed queries from planner, partitioned by source preference
1642:             web_q, acad_q, exa_q = _partition_seeds(sub_queries)
1643:         else:
1644:             # FIX: Wrap LLM analysis in asyncio timeout to prevent hung HTTP calls
1645:             try:
1646:                 analysis = await asyncio.wait_for(
1647:                     _agentic_round_analysis(
1648:                         client=client,
1649:                         original_query=original_query,
1650:                         latest_results=all_web[-50:] + all_academic[-20:],
1651:                         round_summaries=round_summaries,
1652:                         perspective_hits=perspective_hits,
1653:                         round_number=round_num,
1654:                         research_notebook=research_notebook,
1655:                     ),
1656:                     timeout=PG_AGENTIC_ANALYSIS_TIMEOUT_SECONDS,
1657:                 )
1658:             except asyncio.TimeoutError:
1659:                 logger.warning(
1660:                     "[polaris graph] Agentic analysis timed out after %ds "
1661:                     "at round %d — stopping search loop",
1662:                     PG_AGENTIC_ANALYSIS_TIMEOUT_SECONDS, round_num,
1663:                 )
1664:                 break
1665:             last_analysis = analysis
1666: 
1667:             if not analysis.should_continue and round_num > PG_AGENTIC_MIN_ROUNDS:
1668:                 # Check multi-signal convergence
1669:                 converged, reason = _compute_convergence(
1670:                     round_summaries, perspective_hits, analysis,
1671:                     research_notebook=research_notebook,
1672:                 )
1673:                 if converged:
1674:                     logger.info(
1675:                         "[polaris graph] Agentic loop: converged after %d rounds — %s",
1676:                         round_num - 1, reason,
1677:                     )
1678:                     break

1680:             web_q = analysis.web_queries[:PG_AGENTIC_WEB_PER_ROUND]
1681:             acad_q = analysis.academic_queries[:PG_AGENTIC_ACADEMIC_PER_ROUND]
1682:             exa_q = analysis.exa_queries[:PG_AGENTIC_EXA_PER_ROUND]

1: # POLARIS Q1 Launch Readiness — Capability Audit vs Frontier DR (#941)
2: 
3: Source: Claude Codex Workflow `q1-capability-readiness-audit` (6 grounded investigation agents +
4: synthesis), 2026-05-29. Pending Codex §-1.1 verification of load-bearing claims.
5: 
6: **OVERALL VERDICT: READY-WITH-GAPS** — POLARIS's audit-grade per-sentence faithfulness wedge is real,
7: live, and ahead of frontier DR; but the launch path (Pipeline A / `run_honest_sweep_r3.py`) is
8: disconnected from POLARIS's own frontier-grade depth and memory machinery, capped at ~20 sources, and
9: its conflict/memory layers are thin or dormant. The differentiator is shippable; the depth-parity story
10: is an INTEGRATION gap, not a capability gap.
11: 
12: ## Concern 1 — Search Depth: GAP
13: - Flagship tirzepatide fired 41 Serper + 41 S2 searches but `fetch=20`, `corpus.count=20`
14:   (`manifest.json`). `PG_SWEEP_FETCH_CAP=20` (`run_honest_sweep_r3.py:1591-1593`) collapses everything.
15: - POLARIS's real depth engines — the 150-cap citation-snowball `evidence_deepener.py` and the
16:   12-round/~96-query agentic searcher with STORM — are wired ONLY into Pipeline B `graph.py`; grep finds
17:   zero references in the launch sweep. No clinical backend (`domain_backends.py:377` "clinical: rely on
18:   generic Serper + S2"; no PubMed/ClinicalTrials.gov/Cochrane).
19: - vs Frontier: materially behind on raw depth (frontier ingests 50-200+ with iterative deepening) — but
20:   it's an INTEGRATION gap; the machinery exists, just not on the path that ships.
21: 
22: ## Concern 2 — Tool-Usage Tracking: PARTIAL
23: - `pathB_capture.py:142-151` `record_retrieval_attempt` stores only backend NAME strings in a set
24:   (presence flag). The 41+41+19 calls are not individually recorded with query/return-count/URLs.
25: - No per-call `retrieval_trace.jsonl` mirroring the per-call `reasoning_trace.jsonl` LLM roles get.
26:   Dropped candidates (~424 of 444) + fetch failures are aggregate scalars; kept sources have no backend
27:   field; per-query terms exist only transiently on stdout.
28: - vs Frontier: GAP on retrieval transparency; AHEAD on LLM-role provenance. Cannot prove a backend call
29:   returned the source it cites — a §-1.1 line-by-line gap.
30: 
31: ## Concern 3 — Search Credit/Quota: PARTIAL
32: - Live probe: Serper `/search` 200 (`x-ratelimit-remaining=499/500`, refilling), S2 200. Both
33:   gate-mandatory backends (`pathB_run_gate.py:34`) live; no required key missing in `.env`.
34: - No programmatic check of Serper's TOTAL prepaid pool (header is a refilling window counter, not
35:   lifetime credits). `pg_preflight.py` T03 hard-fails on missing `EXA_API_KEY` though Exa is Pipeline-B-
36:   only — preflight isn't a faithful mirror of benchmark creds.
37: - vs Frontier: operational/sustainability difference, not quality. 5-question run ≈ 25-75 Serper calls —
38:   a non-issue; at scale the finite Serper pool is the one throttle frontier indexes lack. One-time manual
39:   dashboard check before launch.
40: 
41: ## Concern 4 — Surface Source Disagreement: PARTIAL
42: - `contradiction_detector.py:575-651` is the SOLE conflict surfacer in Pipeline A — runs unconditionally
43:   (`run_honest_sweep_r3.py:2075-2087`), writes `contradictions.json`, forces both-sides disclosure. Does
44:   NOT silently collapse to one number.
45: - Numeric-regex ONLY → qualitative/directional conflicts (contraindication present-vs-absent, interaction
46:   warnings, eligibility) are structurally invisible. Precision 0/3 on the one real query (all flags were
47:   endpoint/dose grouping artifacts the report itself apologizes for). The 4-role gate is a per-claim
48:   grounding gate (off by default), not a conflict surfacer.
49: - vs Frontier: AHEAD on intent/honesty; undermined by thin, noisy, numeric-only detection blind to the
50:   qualitative clinical conflicts that hurt patients.
51: 
52: ## Concern 5 — Report Quality: PARTIAL
53: - `verification_details.json` is a real per-sentence VERIFIED/DROPPED+reason ledger backed by the 6-check
54:   `provenance_generator.py:896-1290` verifier — no frontier DR ships this; it caught real fabrications.
55: - Verified core is THIN — 38 verified vs 35 dropped (~48% kept; docstring admits ~73% typical drop).
56:   Frontier-comparable length (3828 words) carried by the explicitly-UNVERIFIED Analyst Synthesis layer,
57:   which leaked a dangling `[ev_012]` citation into published `report.md:61` (scrub regex
58:   `analyst_synthesis.py:107` only matches `[#ev:...]`, not bare `[ev_NNN]`). Verifier over-drops correct
59:   prose (a fully-framed SURPASS-2 sentence dropped on a literal title-token miss).
60: - vs Frontier: WINS on auditability, COMPETITIVE on structure, TRAILS on verified-narrative depth.
61: 
62: ## Concern 6 — Semantic Memory: GAP
63: - `verified_claim_graph.py:185-213` `query_related_claims` + `find_contradictions` are referenced ONLY by
64:   the store + its tests; nothing in `src/` reads the pool back into generation. The KG is WRITE-ONLY —
65:   zero snowball reuse at runtime. Flat SQLite table, NO edges (relatedness = lexical keyword overlap, not
66:   embeddings). Only writer is guarded default-OFF, runs only against a fake transport offline. Pipeline A
67:   imports no memory module. Agent-side: `MEMORY.md` is 40.2KB over a 24.4KB load limit, truncates today.
68: - vs Frontier: differentiated CONCEPT (frontier is stateless) but UNWIRED — zero runtime edge today.
69: 
70: ## ORDERED Pre-Q1 Fix List
71: ### Tier A — No-spend code fixes (convert dormant capability into shipped capability)
72: 1. Wire `evidence_deepener.py` (citation snowball, 150-cap) into the launch path. Highest leverage. (C1)
73: 2. Raise `PG_SWEEP_FETCH_CAP` from 20 to 50-100+ and re-tune MAX_SERPER/MAX_S2. (C1)
74: 3. Add a qualitative/directional conflict path to the detector (`(did not|no|never|absent|without) +
75:    endpoint vocab → require atom OR escalate to LLM judge`). (C4)
76: 4. Emit per-call `retrieval_trace.jsonl` (per query: backend/text/return-count/URLs; per kept source:
77:    backend; per drop: URL+reason). (C2)
78: 5. Fix the citation-integrity leak — scrub bare `[ev_NNN]` too, or resolve to bibliography. (C5)
79: 6. Loosen verifier trial-name matching to evidence body/snippet, not just `title`. (C5)
80: 7. Fix preflight T03 honesty — drop Exa from Pipeline-A scope OR wire Exa into `live_retriever.py`. (C3)
81: 8. Wire the KG read path — call `query_related_claims` back into generation. (C6)
82: 9. Trim `MEMORY.md` under the 24.4KB budget. (C6)
83: 10. Add an executive-summary / key-findings-up-front block to the report. (C5)
84: 
85: ### Tier B — Operator / spend-gated
86: 1. Manual Serper dashboard check before launch (prepaid pool not header-visible). (C3)
87: 2. Procure/wire a dedicated clinical backend (PubMed E-utilities — `NCBI_API_KEY` already present —
88:    ClinicalTrials.gov, Cochrane). (C1, C3)
89: 3. Operator-authorize the Gate-B 4-role canary against a live endpoint (so the per-claim gate + KG write
90:    actually execute in the shipped path). (C4, C6)
91: 4. Validate the entailment judge's precision/recall on a labeled set (18 of 53 drops this run). (C5)
92: 5. (Stretch) Embedding-based KG relatedness + claim edges (ChromaDB `cross_vector.py` is a start). (C6)
93: 
94: **Bottom line:** the wedge that wins Carney — auditable per-sentence faithfulness — is real and ahead of
95: frontier today. What blocks an unqualified READY is that POLARIS's own best depth/memory machinery is
96: sitting one import away from the launch path. Tier A 1-3 are the difference between "competitive on
97: safety, behind on depth" and "beats the frontier on both."
